   <div id="CHEMINF_000433"></div>
   <div id="HenrysLawConstant"></div>

HenrysLawConstant
^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^

.. raw:: html

  <table class="element-table">
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">IRI</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href='#CHEMINF_000433' onclick="if(!document.getElementById('CHEMINF_000433')){window.location.href='http://semanticscience.org/resource/CHEMINF_000433'; return false;}">http://semanticscience.org/resource/CHEMINF_000433</a></td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-annotations" colspan="2">Annotations</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">prefLabel</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">HenrysLawConstant</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">definition</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">Henry's law, formulated by William Henry in 1803, states "At a constant temperature, the amount of a given gas that dissolves in a given type and volume of liquid is directly proportional to the partial pressure of that gas in equilibrium with that liquid." Henry's law can be put into mathematical terms (at constant temperature) as<br>    p = kHc<br>where p is the partial pressure of the solute in the gas above the solution, c is the concentration of the solute and kH is a constant with the dimensions of pressure divided by concentration. The constant, known as the Henry's law constant, depends on the solute, the solvent and the temperature.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-formal-description" colspan="2">Formal description</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">subClassOf</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href='#CHEMINF_000025' onclick="if(!document.getElementById('CHEMINF_000025')){window.location.href='http://semanticscience.org/resource/CHEMINF_000025'; return false;}">PhysicalDescriptor</a></td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Restrictions</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><div class="restriction-list"><ul><li><a href='http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000136'>isAbout</a> some <a href='#CHEMINF_000266' onclick="if(!document.getElementById('CHEMINF_000266')){window.location.href='http://semanticscience.org/resource/CHEMINF_000266'; return false;}">ChemicalSubstance</a></li></ul></div></td>
  </tr>
  </table>

  </table>

    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">prefLabel</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">InChIWithFixedHLayer</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">definition</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">An InChI descriptor that is not the standard and that is created with the fixedH layer option. The fixedH layer is appended to the standard InChI and lists the exact position of the tautomeric hydrogen atoms. It is useful when one wants to represent a specific tautomer of a given structure, because if the InChIs for the tautomers were created without the fixedH layer option, the normalization performed by the InChI generation program would result in these InChIs being identical.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">source</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href='https://doi.org/10.1186%2Fs13321-015-0068-4'>https://doi.org/10.1186%2Fs13321-015-0068-4</a></td>
  </tr>

    <th class="element-table-formal-description" colspan="2">Formal description</th>
  </tr>

  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">altLabel</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">petitjeanNumber</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">definition</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">the eccentricity of a vertex corresponds to the distance from that vertex to the most remote vertex in the graph. The distance is obtained from the distance matrix as the count of edges between the two vertices. If r i is the largest matrix entry in row i of the distance matrix D, then the radius is defined as the smallest of the r i . The graph diameter D is defined as the largest vertex eccentricity in the graph. Petitjean Number is the value of ( diameter - radius ) diameter .</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-formal-description" colspan="2">Formal description</th>

   <div id="CHEMINF_000520"></div>
   <div id="RelativeConfigurationStereochemicalDescriptor"></div>

RelativeConfigurationStereochemicalDescriptor
^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^

.. raw:: html

  <table class="element-table">
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">IRI</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href='#CHEMINF_000520' onclick="if(!document.getElementById('CHEMINF_000520')){window.location.href='http://semanticscience.org/resource/CHEMINF_000520'; return false;}">http://semanticscience.org/resource/CHEMINF_000520</a></td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-annotations" colspan="2">Annotations</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">prefLabel</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">RelativeConfigurationStereochemicalDescriptor</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">definition</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">The configuration of any stereogenic (asymmetric) centre with respect to any other stereogenic centre contained within the same molecular entity. Unlike absolute configuration, relative configuration is reflection-invariant. Relative configuration, distinguishing diastereoisomers, may be denoted by the configurational descriptors R*, R* (or l) and R*, S* (or u) meaning, respectively, that the two centres have identical or opposite configurations. For molecules with more than two asymmetric centres the prefix rel- may be used in front of the name of one enantiomer where R and S have been used. If any centres have known absolute configuration then only R* and S* can be used for the relative configuration.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">source</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href='https://doi.org/10.1351/goldbook.R05260'>https://doi.org/10.1351/goldbook.R05260</a></td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-formal-description" colspan="2">Formal description</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">subClassOf</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href='#CHEMINF_000027' onclick="if(!document.getElementById('CHEMINF_000027')){window.location.href='http://semanticscience.org/resource/CHEMINF_000027'; return false;}">StereochemicalDescriptor</a></td>

    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Subclasses</span></td>
